# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox CSS calc() Value Overflow

## Your Task

Firefox crashes when processing CSS calc() with extreme values. Find the C++ source files in mozilla/gecko-dev that (1) parse CSS calc() expressions and (2) handle numeric overflow during calc() value resolution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

73-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Firefox gecko-dev codebase and identified the C++ and Rust source files responsible for CSS calc() parsing and numeric overflow handling. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

**The Firefox crash occurs due to unprotected floating-point arithmetic during CSS calc() value resolution.** The vulnerability spans from parsing through computed value resolution.

### Files Identified:

1. **CSS calc() Parsing**: `servo/components/style/values/specified/calc.rs`
   - Parses CSS calc() expressions and mathematical functions

2. **Calc Expression Tree**: `servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs`  
   - Defines the generic `GenericCalcNode` AST structure
   - Contains `resolve_internal()` and `resolve_map()` that perform arithmetic

3. **Critical Overflow Points**: `servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs`
   - `CalcLengthPercentageLeaf::try_sum_in_place()` - plain `+=` without overflow check
   - `CalcLengthPercentageLeaf::try_product_in_place()` - plain `*=` without bounds check
   - `CalcLengthPercentage::resolve()` - applies clamping but only AFTER overflow

4. **Clamping (Post-Overflow)**: `servo/components/style_traits/values.rs`
   - `AllowedNumericType::clamp()` - cannot recover from infinity/NaN

5. **FFI Bridge**: `servo/ports/geckolib/glue.rs`
   - `Servo_ResolveCalcLengthPercentage()` - exposes vulnerable Rust code to C++

6. **C++ Integration**: `layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h`
   - `StyleCalcLengthPercentage::Resolve()` and `ResolveToCSSPixels()` - call the FFI

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, and a detailed explanation of the vulnerability chain.

This generic structure is used for both specified and computed values.\\n\\n## Numeric Overflow Issues\\n\\n### Root Cause: Unprotected Arithmetic in Computed Values\\nThe critical overflow vulnerability occurs in `servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs` in the `CalcLengthPercentageLeaf` trait implementation:\\n\\n1. **try_sum_in_place()** (line 796-832): Performs addition with plain `+=` operator (line 815) without overflow checking. For example:\\n   ```rust\\n   *one += *other;  // Plain float addition, can overflow to infinity\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **try_product_in_place()** (line 834-858): Performs multiplication with plain `*=` operator (line 838) without bounds checking:\\n   ```rust\\n   *left *= *right;  // Plain float multiplication, can overflow\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **try_op()** (line 860-883): Applies arbitrary operations to leaf values, including the result at line 870:\\n   ```rust\\n   Length(super::Length::new(op(one.px(), other.px())))  // op can produce infinity/NaN\\n   ```\\n\\n4. **map()** (line 885-897): Applies a function to leaf values without validation of the result.\\n\\n### Resolution Chain\\nThe resolution process in `GenericCalcNode::resolve_internal()` (`servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs`, line 928) performs arithmetic operations without overflow protection:\\n\\n- Line 950: `result = result.try_op(&right, |left, right| left + right)?;` for Sum nodes\\n- Line 965/971: `result.map(|v| v * left)?;` for Product nodes\\n\\nThese operations chain together, and when extreme values are provided in calc() expressions (e.g., `calc(10e308 * 10e308)`), they produce infinity or NaN values.\\n\\n### Clamping Limitations\\nWhile `AllowedNumericType::clamp()` in `servo/components/style_traits/values.rs` (lines 593-599) provides post-computation clamping, it only clamps based on the allowed numeric type (All, NonNegative, AtLeastOne, ZeroToOne). This clamping happens AFTER overflow has already occurred:\\n\\n```rust\\nLength::new(self.clamping_mode.clamp(px.px())).normalized()  // Line 1004 in length_percentage.rs\\n```\\n\\nOnce a value has overflowed to infinity, `clamp()` cannot recover the original intent.\\n\\n## C++ Integration Points\\n\\nThe Servo Rust code integrates with C++ Firefox through:\\n\\n1. **FFI Gateway** (`servo/ports/geckolib/glue.rs`, line 9208):\\n   ```rust\\n   pub extern \\\"C\\\" fn Servo_ResolveCalcLengthPercentage(\\n       calc: &computed::length_percentage::CalcLengthPercentage,\\n       basis: f32,\\n   ) -> f32 {\\n       calc.resolve(computed::Length::new(basis)).px()  // Calls resolve() which can overflow\\n   }\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **C++ Resolution** (`layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h`, lines 726-735):\\n   ```cpp\\n   CSSCoord StyleCalcLengthPercentage::ResolveToCSSPixels(CSSCoord aBasis) const {\\n       return Servo_ResolveCalcLengthPercentage(this, aBasis);
